always be so death by axe be doom awarded to by king day appointed for execution be friday th of may at hour of noon leaving conduct of fatal ceremony to duke of suffolk who have order to have signal gun fired from summit of white tower be to be answered from various point when be over henry repaired to windsor castle on evening of thursday before have formally offered hand to jane seymour while unfortunate queen be languishing within tower be basking in smile of new mistress counting hour till must make own on tuesday before execution jane seymour retired to father mansion wolff hall in wiltshire where preparation be made for marriage be arranged must take place there in private on saturday on arriving at castle henry gave out that must hunt on following morning in great park retired to closet did not long remain there putting on garb of yeoman of guard descended by narrow flight of step already mentioned a occupying same situation a existing hundred step to town proceeded to garter where found several guest assembled discussing affair of day bryan bowntance strong ale at same time amongst number be duke of shoreditch paddington hector cutbeard kit coo at moment of king entrance be talking of approaching execution oh vanity of worldly greatness exclaimed bryan lifting up hand only seven year ago last saint george day lovely queen first entered castle with king amid pomp splendour power with long life apparently of happiness before now be condemned to die if have played king false deserves doom replied shoreditch must behead own wife if served same trick be if must do right to say 'if must ' rejoined paddington beheading of wife be royal privilege can not be enjoyed by subject marry wonder how king must prefer mistress jane seymour for part said hector cutbeard to thinking be not to be compared with queen anne have lovely blue eye figure a straight a arrow returned shoreditch how say master added turning to king what think of mistress jane seymour that be passably fair friend replied henry how a compared with late be present queen for poor soul have yet hour to live rejoined shoreditch how a compared with why think jane seymour more lovely undoubtedly replied henry may be prejudiced not in least friend said cutbeard partake of royal master humour jane seymour be beautiful doubt so be anne boleyn marry will see many fair queen on throne royal henry have good taste good management set subject rare example show how to get rid of troublesome wife will divorce hang spouse when get tired of almost wish be married might try experiment have have well here be king health cried shoreditch wishing a many wife a may desire what say friend added turning to henry will not drink that toast will replied henry fancy king will be content for present with mistress jane seymour for present doubt said hector cutbeard time will come ere long when jane will be a irksome to a anne be now ah god death knave darest thou say so cried henry furiously why have said nothing treasonable hope rejoined cutbeard turning pale only wish king to be happy in own way a seems to delight in change of wife pray that may have to heart content fair explanation replied henry laughing let give health master cried tall archer whom one have hitherto noticed rising in one corner of room be headsman of calais may do work featly tomorrow have have have good toast cried hector cutbeard seize who have proposed cried king rising be herne hunter laugh at threat here a elsewhere harry cried herne will meet tomorrow flinging horn cup in face of man nearest sprang through open window at back disappeared cutbeard shoreditch be much alarmed lest freedom of expression must be taken in umbrage by king calmed fear by bestowing good humoured buffet on cheek of latter of quitting hostel returned to castle by same way have left on following morning about ten o'clock rode into great park attended by numerous train demeanour be moody stern general gloom pervaded company keeping on western side of park party crossed cranbourne chase though encountered several fine herd of deer king gave order to uncouple hound at last arrived at part of park where sandpit gate be now situated pursuing path bordered by noble tree fine buck be suddenly unharboured upon henry gave order to huntsman others to follow adding that must proceed to snow hill where must find hour hence understood why king wished to be alone for what purpose be about to repair to eminence in question therefore without word whole company started off in chase meanwhile king rode slowly through wood often pausing to listen to distant sound of hunter noticing shadow on greensward a grew shorter proclaimed approach of noon at length arrived at snow hill stationed beneath tree on summit from point magnificent view of castle towering over pomp of wood now covered with foliage of most vivid green be commanded morning be bright beautiful sky cloudless gentle rain have fallen over night have tempered air freshened leaf greensward bird be singing blithely in tree at foot of hill crouched herd of deer be genial delightful breathing of tenderness peace calculated to soften most obdurate heart scene be not without effect upon henry fierce tumult raged within breast fixed eye on round tower be distinctly visible from expected signal then tried to peer into far horizon must discern nothing cloud passed over sun cast momentary gloom over smiling landscape at same time henry fancy be so powerfully excited that fancied must behold terrible tragedy enacting at tower be now issuing forth into green in front of saint peter chapel said henry to can see a distinctly a if be there ah how beautiful look how move heart to pity suffolk richmond cromwell lord mayor be there to meet take leave of weeping attendant mount step of scaffold firmly look round address spectator how silent be how clearly musically voice sound blesses hear feel here now disrobes prepares for fatal axe be wielded by skilful executioner of calais be now feeling edge now take leave of dame bestows parting gift on again kneel prays rise fatal moment be at hand even now retains courage approach block place head upon axe be raised exclamation be occasioned by flash of fire from battlement of round tower followed by volume of smoke in second deep boom of gun be heard at very moment that flash be seen wild figure mounted on coal black steed galloped from out wood dashed towards henry whose horse reared plunged a passed there spoke knell of anne boleyn cried herne regarding henry sternly pointing to round tower bloody deed be done thou art free to wed once more away to wolff hall bring thy new consort to windsor castle thus end sixth last book of chronicle of windsor castle
